  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ea17e923-34bf-461d-8d04-4be328151f08'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1578289390i/31968163._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/31968163-the-overflowing-inkwell">The Overflowing Inkwell</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Not quite. There are bits left out, or they are conveyed in an image without the entire thought process (one that comes to mind is the scene where Bel<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Not quite. There are bits left out, or they are conveyed in an image without the entire thought process (one that comes to mind is the scene where Bella first sits beside Edward in Biology class, and wonders why he is looking at her so oddly; she sniffs her hair thinking she might smell odd - in the Graphic Novel, she sits beside him, he looks at her oddly, she sniffs her hair. Without reading the book first, it would probably still leave a lot of questions. My sister who hasn't read Twilight before is looking at it this second and is thinking that it's very jerky in spots.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4127700930852485182"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/> <br/>You know what's embarrassing? Going into a thrift store when you're almost thirty years of age and buying Twilight: The Graphic Novel while the teenage male cashier judges you.<br/><br/><br/><br/>WHATEVER, TEENAGE MALE CASHIER. I REGRET NOTHING. AND NOW I HAVE TWILIGHT: THE GRAPHIC NOVEL AND YOU DON'T. SO I WIN.<br/><br/><br/><br/>When this book first came out in 2010, my first thought was, "Are you kidding me?" It looked like a cash grab to capitalize off the movie. <i>Twilight</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4127700930852485182" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br> <br>You know what's embarrassing? Going into a thrift store when you're almost thirty years of age and buying Twilight: The Graphic Novel while the teenage male cashier judges you.<br><br><br><br>WHATEVER, TEENAGE MALE CASHIER. I REGRET NOTHING. AND NOW I HAVE TWILIGHT: THE GRAPHIC NOVEL AND YOU DON'T. SO I WIN.<br><br><br><br>When this book first came out in 2010, my first thought was, "Are you kidding me?" It looked like a cash grab to capitalize off the movie. <i>Twilight </i>mania was in full swing and you literally could not go anywhere without hearing someone talk about it. I initially liked the books, but the movies and the fans turned me off the series so fast because there was no escape.<br><br><br><br>NO ESCAPE. <br><br><br><br>Well, now that I've read the book for myself, I have revised this opinion. Yes, it is a graphic novel of a book that was turned into a movie <i>but</i>... the art is beautiful. Young Kim did such an amazing job. The expressions, the use of color... even the <i>text </i>they used... it's all so gorgeous, and fits the tone of the story far better than the movie ever did. I feel like the scenery and the looks of the characters were much more true to form.<br><br><br><br>You may be asking yourself, "What's the point?" Well, if you enjoyed TWILIGHT and you're the type of person who would buy one of those Harlequin manga (yes, they exist; yes they are awesome - YOU WOULD BE SO AMAZED HOW WELL ROMANCE TRANSLATES TO MANGA), then you should definitely get this book for your collection. I know it's going to stay in mine. &lt;3<br><br><br><br>I kind of want to revisit the novel now. It's been sitting on my dresser, waiting...<br><br><br><br>5 stars</span>

<div id="review_2295955542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2295955542" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2295955542?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2295955542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16533942809850311229">Hahahahahahaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaa… I’ve always wondered what getting dosed with Joker Toxin was like - and now I know! <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518632245i/25060475._SX540_.png' width='600' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Oooooooooooooooh kay. So: a disclaimer to start with for those wunnering what the hey am I doing reading Twilight The Graphic Novel in the first place. Your instincts are right: it wasn’t my idea! It’s my totally disproportionate punishment for making <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1720620-anne' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anne</a> read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24819813-vader?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vader</a>, as suggested by<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/39811979-artemy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Artemy</a> (yeah, don’t think I forgot it was your idea in the first place, you wily Russian!), and it’s t</span>
  <span id="freeText16533942809850311229" style="display:none">Hahahahahahaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaa… I’ve always wondered what getting dosed with Joker Toxin was like - and now I know! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518632245i/25060475._SX540_.png" width="600" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oooooooooooooooh kay. So: a disclaimer to start with for those wunnering what the hey am I doing reading Twilight The Graphic Novel in the first place. Your instincts are right: it wasn’t my idea! It’s my totally disproportionate punishment for making <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1720620-anne" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne</a> read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24819813-vader?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Vader</a>, as suggested by<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/39811979-artemy" rel="nofollow noopener">Artemy</a> (yeah, don’t think I forgot it was your idea in the first place, you wily Russian!), and it’s totally unfair. Vader is a solid three star read – Twilight – FUCKING TWILIGHT!!! - was only ever going to be a solid dogshit read! <br><br>But you humour the elderly, don’t you? Especially the batty ones, bless. Plus it’s Valentine’s Day which means… something to someone, somewhere. And for those involved in insisting this happen – <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/25388909-chad" rel="nofollow noopener">you</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3461034-trish" rel="nofollow noopener">know</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2397418-ran" rel="nofollow noopener">who</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1776702-mike" rel="nofollow noopener">you</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12618229-jeff" rel="nofollow noopener">are</a> – as well as the aforementioned, consider this my anti-valentine’s to all youse slobs! <br>(And a special tip of the hat to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2397418-ran" rel="nofollow noopener">Ran</a> for making the awesome banner above - I highly recommend reading her reviews; she’s one of the good ones.)<br><br>So, here it is. Take it away, Heath! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445290496ra/16625101.gif" width="648" height="264" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Once upon a time… a vampire, a werewolf and an idiot formed a love triangle and made a Mormon housewife a multi-millionaire. <br><br>It sounds like the setup to a joke – except there’s no punchline (unless you count getting rope-a-doped into reading it)! I don’t think I need to summarise the plot any further as bloody everyone knows the stupid story of Twilight even though if you’ve got a penus chances are you haven’t read it. Team Edward, Team Jacob – I was always (and staunchly remain) Team Who Gives A Flying Fuck?! <br><br>And right away the whole mess falls apart because at no point is it convincing that Bella the idiot is going to go for anyone but Dead Ed – Jacob Abs is always the useless third wheel. <br><br>I just caught myself there for a moment: I’m actually bothering to critique Twilight in detail. It’s like having to explain why painting your junk red and jiggling them in front of a bull is a bad idea. Everyone already knows this crap is, well, crap! Alright, let’s just white knuckle this sucker and get the hell out of dodge!<br><br>So let’s talk about Edward Cullen, aka Shovel Face (gawd bless those <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0gugBiEkLwU" rel="nofollow noopener">Honest Trailers</a>), the sole reason why this drek got so unfathomably popular in the first place. <br><br>Edward’s not a vampire. He can walk about in the daytime and all that shizness about garlic, crosses and coffins is out the window. He likes blood (but he’s “vegetarian” as he only drinks animal blood, not human, ohohoho, my fucking sides are a-splitting), is immortally young and he can move fast. That’s not a vampire. Oh and he SPARKLES during the twilight hour of the day! Wh… WHY?! Is that what women want: their blokes to literally light up like a fucking Christmas tree when the sun sets?! If he’s a vampire I’m Martha Stewart. <br><br>Really: what’s so appealing about this personality vacuum?? He’s generically good-looking – is that all? Is it because he’s over a hundred years old but he looks perpetually 15, a mixture of (supposed) wisdom and beauty? I guess the forbidden fruit angle or something lame like that. God, some people are so easy to please! <br><br>Maybe it’s explained in the novel proper but I have no idea why Edward goes to high school in the first place. The last thing I’d do as a vampire is waste my time attending some shitty Midwest high school! No clue either what he sees in Bella, the blankest of blank slates. Or what Bella sees in Edward for that matter. Sigh… contrived romance, thy name is Twilight. <br><br>Buhh… almost there… <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518616641ra/25059047.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nothing happens in this book. Bella goes dress shopping, goes to dinner, faints during biology class, goes on a camping trip where she meets Personality Vacuum #2 aka Jacob, wonders moronically whether Edward’s really a vampire or a superhero, there’s the hint of a mugging – that scene was so poorly written/drawn and rushed that it wasn’t clear what was going on or why. This book is over 200 pages long! <br><br>The dialogue in general is too dull to bear repeating but this clunky line in particular really spoke to me. Ed’s just saved Bella from a mugging(?), then suddenly starts flapping and says: "Before I turn around and hunt down those.. just prattle about something unimportant until I calm down!" I felt like saying “Oh! Hey, Edward, here’s an entire book full of garbage that fulfils exactly that purpose!!”<br><br>Artist Young Kim draws the book manga-style because women comics readers predominantly tend to read manga and the publisher knows that this comic’s audience is gonna be mostly women. I guess it’s skilful – I can’t talk, I can just about manage stickmen! – though all the characters look like mindless kawaii dolls. <br><br>Alright, let’s wrap a bow on this turd! <br><br>I’ll be honest. I could pretend and say this was the worst comic I’ve ever read but I’ve been reading Marvel and DC comics for years and as a result have built up quite a high threshold for painfully bad books. But Twilight: The Graphic Novel, Volume 1 is still down there. It’s an unoriginal waste of time - a plotless, inane, and unconvincing pseudo-romance full of bland non-characters vapidly and meaninglessly in love. Like most pop culture at this level (think the Transformers movies and Fidget Spinners), I was bored and annoyed the entire time and found the whole thing drearily pathetic. The book would’ve been vastly improved with a character there purely to slap the others for being twats. Know what else sparkles? A brass knuckle sammich! <br><br>HAPPY VALENTINE’S MUTHAFUCKAS!!!!1<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518616641ra/25059048.gif" width="500" height="243" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16533942809850311229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030902975?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030902975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10447868235421924650">I don't even know why I bothered with this, but I will concede that the artwork to this graphic novel is intricate, detailed and very dazzling. The <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_' title='Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twilight</a> story in and of itself is still equally as awful in illustrated form as it is in plain text though, so I really hope the artist who created the graphics for this book finds a better platform for their beautiful talent.</span>
  <span id="freeText10447868235421924650" style="display:none">I don't even know why I bothered with this, but I will concede that the artwork to this graphic novel is intricate, detailed and very dazzling. The <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> story in and of itself is still equally as awful in illustrated form as it is in plain text though, so I really hope the artist who created the graphics for this book finds a better platform for their beautiful talent.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10779718084212845922">You should know that I was a fangirl at the time Twilight hit cinemas. I read all the books, saw all the movies and was very much in love with the series in the beginning. I hadn't read much YA up until that point, so I wasn't really aware of all the tropes. Also, I didn't care about the 100+ years old stalker/pedophile. It was all very romantic to me. I wanted a love all consuming, like Bella and Edward had. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49041.New_Moon__Twilight___2_' title='New Moon (Twilight, #2) by Stephenie Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>New Moon</a> was torture for me because it kept them apart. It's my least favorite book in </span>
  <span id="freeText10779718084212845922" style="display:none">You should know that I was a fangirl at the time Twilight hit cinemas. I read all the books, saw all the movies and was very much in love with the series in the beginning. I hadn't read much YA up until that point, so I wasn't really aware of all the tropes. Also, I didn't care about the 100+ years old stalker/pedophile. It was all very romantic to me. I wanted a love all consuming, like Bella and Edward had. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49041.New_Moon__Twilight___2_" title="New Moon (Twilight, #2) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">New Moon</a> was torture for me because it kept them apart. It's my least favorite book in the series.<br /><br />So reading this graphic novel is all about nostalgia for me. It's me trying to recapture that feeling I had for the franchise in the beginning. You know, I actually get butterflies in my stomach from great book romances. The graphic novel didn't necessarily give me that feeling, but it helped me remember how I first fell in love with the Twilight phenomenon.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer94244901" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6530609202376497186">Anyone familiar with graphic novels knows they don't take long to read. I read it three times within the given time period. It's only volume one, through the meadow scene. I don't know if the rest of the story wasn't finished in time for publishing, or if more than one volume was planned. I can't wait to have the rest.<br/><br/>The illustrations are beautifully rendered and so representative of the written descriptions. Color is used sparingly, and enhances the scene or feeling. The written story is abbre</span>
  <span id="freeText6530609202376497186" style="display:none">Anyone familiar with graphic novels knows they don't take long to read. I read it three times within the given time period. It's only volume one, through the meadow scene. I don't know if the rest of the story wasn't finished in time for publishing, or if more than one volume was planned. I can't wait to have the rest.<br /><br />The illustrations are beautifully rendered and so representative of the written descriptions. Color is used sparingly, and enhances the scene or feeling. The written story is abbreviated, not giving as much of Bella's thoughts, but enough to communicate her personality. Edward is also well communicated, in the drawings, the written physical actions, and of course in his words, which I'll reiterate is faithful to the novel. <br /><br />I highly recommend it to any fan. I'm curious if it brings in new readers. </span>

My grandmother walking into my room and telling me that reading for four hours straight is not good for my eyes and that sooner or later my body will require food;<br/><br/>2. I was so obsessed with Kristin Stewart that I dyed my hair auburn, purchased the same gray dress she wore for a Much Music interview--all for my grad photos!;<br/><br/>3.   <span id="freeText16670505095454863313" style="display:none">Yup, I read this. Don't you dare judge me. <i>*narrows eyes*</i><br><br><b>My most nostalgic Twilight memories as a teen:</b><br><br><blockquote>1. My grandmother walking into my room and telling me that reading for four hours straight is not good for my eyes and that sooner or later my body will require food;<br><br>2. I was so obsessed with Kristin Stewart that I dyed my hair auburn, purchased the same gray dress she wore for a Much Music interview--all for my grad photos!;<br><br>3. In grade 12, I snuck into a movie theatre with the help of some badass friends because tickets to the last movie were sold out. Obvs I wasn't about to let that stop me or the law for that matter; and (finally)<br><br>4. The beautiful New Moon poster on my bedroom wall. (#RIP, it didn't survive the move to my new home)</blockquote><br><br>Alright, let's get down to the nitty-gritty of things.<br><br>Is this a literary masterpiece? Of course not. But it's definitely a guilty pleasure of mine! It's replete with insta-love, cringe-worthy scenes, and sparkly vampires.<br><br>I do, however, prefer the graphic novel adaptation over the movies and original books. Why? Most of the awkward scenes are omitted and hold your panties, Bella is LESS annoying too. OHMYGAH.<br><br>I immensely enjoyed the art work as well. A good portion of the novel is black and white, but I loved how the reader was given a burst of colour every now and then. The illustrations of Edward were so swoon-worthy that I felt myself starting to fall for him all over again. <br><br><i>

<div id="review_87350312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87350312" />
    <a title="Bry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1360862-bry"><img alt="Bry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589172666p2/1360862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87350312?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bry" href="/user/show/1360862-bry">Bry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87350312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12456043579950524155">Right off the bat I love the colors in this book. Most of the book is this wonderfully muted near black and white coloring, yet a lot of pages has just the slightest hint of a single color that adds a lot of depth to the 2D drawings. <br/><br/>Furthermore the art itself is beautiful with all of its details. Even the backgrounds are highly detailed, and each page makes sure to use almost every square inch available. At least this is true when the humans are the subjects of the page. The art becomes incredi</span>
  <span id="freeText12456043579950524155" style="display:none">Right off the bat I love the colors in this book. Most of the book is this wonderfully muted near black and white coloring, yet a lot of pages has just the slightest hint of a single color that adds a lot of depth to the 2D drawings. <br /><br />Furthermore the art itself is beautiful with all of its details. Even the backgrounds are highly detailed, and each page makes sure to use almost every square inch available. At least this is true when the humans are the subjects of the page. The art becomes incredibly surreal and dreamy when it focuses on the vampires, and its as if they are all that exist for that moment, that page, and nothing else is important. Some pages the artist took photographs and morphed them into her drawings by sketching over them to blend the 2 images to create a more realistic background (an example of this is when Bella is sitting on the bed in the hospital after nearly being hit by Tyler in the van or the first glimpse of La Push First Beach). Just stunning!<br /><br />The cover art alone is worth drooling over with all of the shading and amazing use of light. <br /><br />I am basing my rating off all of this, or the art, layout, and composition as it were. The pacing and the layout of the drawings keep you turning pages at a furious rate, and I can't wait to go through it again to take in the art a bit more because I am sure that every time you read this you will notice more and more details that went previously unnoticed. <br /><br />My only complaint though is how short it was - not in terms of pages but in how far it actually progressed through the story. I was hoping to at least get to see some interaction between Bella and the other Cullens. But not to worry there are more volumes coming. Although at this point only Twilight has been green lighted for graphic novelization, so I for one am keeping my fingers crossed that Meyer will approve the rest of the saga!<br /><br />This is definitely recommended to any fan of Twilight, whether they have read a graphic novel before or not!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12456043579950524155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94239221" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94239221" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3333280-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266944727p2/3333280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94239221?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/3333280-tatiana">Tatiana</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Twilight fans, teens, graphic novel enthusiasts</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94239221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15487729486609921410">It took one hour to read this magnificent graphic novel, but oh, what a fantastic 60 minutes it was!<br/><br/>SPOILER ALERT!!!!!!!<br/><br/>Let me just say that the artist, Young Kim, is one talented lady, and she has breathed new life into a classic vampire series. She captures the quiet beauty of Bella Swan, making her look lovely, but in an unadorned way that we have always pictured, but have never seen. She combines her own artistry with live shots, and the results are stunning. You feel as if you are truly ste</span>
  <span id="freeText15487729486609921410" style="display:none">It took one hour to read this magnificent graphic novel, but oh, what a fantastic 60 minutes it was!<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT!!!!!!!<br /><br />Let me just say that the artist, Young Kim, is one talented lady, and she has breathed new life into a classic vampire series. She captures the quiet beauty of Bella Swan, making her look lovely, but in an unadorned way that we have always pictured, but have never seen. She combines her own artistry with live shots, and the results are stunning. You feel as if you are truly stepping into the wet and slippery world of Forks, Washington, immersing yourself in a world where humans, werewolves and vampires co-exist unwittingly. What made this graphic novel such a easy page-turner is not just the knock-out drawings, but the layout as well, which is key to the enjoyment of any graphic novel. Kim has been able to give a face to all our favorite characters, and where she resoundingly succeeds is in her depiction of Edward. No slight to the handsome Robert Pattinson, but this is the way I had imagined Edward Cullen to look like - gorgeous and other-worldly in his male beauty. <br /><br />For those of us who know the story like the back of our hand, this first volume concludes with Bella and Edward leaving the forest, with the initial secrets of vampires revealed in their pretty swath of forest. We all know how it starts, where it's going, and how it ends, but my goodness, I cannot wait for the next installment. Let's hope Stephenie Meyer will give her blessing for the three other books, because as of right now, only Twilight is getting the graphic novel treatment. I highly recommend this book to all fans of Twilight, vampire lovers, and reluctant readers who need a more aesthetically pleasing introduction to the world of Bella Swan and Edward Cullen. For grades 5th and up. Enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15487729486609921410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_96297919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96297919" />
    <a title="Maddie Senator" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2782054-maddie-senator"><img alt="Maddie Senator" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417490922p2/2782054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96297919?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie Senator" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie Senator" href="/user/show/2782054-maddie-senator">Maddie Senator</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96297919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13715551555302816293">I was really excited when I learned about the existence of this book because it combines two of my favorite guilty pleasures: Asian graphic novels and Twilight. I have yet to find any artist's rendition of the story (whether it be in film or a drawing) that captures the vivid images I had in my head when I first read the book, but this is a very beautiful version. I really enjoyed the art, although Edward doesn't look right most of the time to me--more like a 50s letterman athlete type or someth</span>
  <span id="freeText13715551555302816293" style="display:none">I was really excited when I learned about the existence of this book because it combines two of my favorite guilty pleasures: Asian graphic novels and Twilight. I have yet to find any artist's rendition of the story (whether it be in film or a drawing) that captures the vivid images I had in my head when I first read the book, but this is a very beautiful version. I really enjoyed the art, although Edward doesn't look right most of the time to me--more like a 50s letterman athlete type or something, and Bella is too pretty. She looks like some glamour queen, when if her looks had been toned down a little she still would have been very attractive but in a more normal way.<br />The fact that the book was in sepia tones except for a few pages when the author added well-placed splashes of color made it very unique and delightful to read and look at. I highly enjoyed it, and it was also nice to get the story in its actual sequence of events; I find myself getting fuzzy on that since I have seen the movie so much now. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13715551555302816293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_105248047" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105248047" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105248047?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105248047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10846783620345291331">You know what, if I'm allowed to be completely and utterly honest - I probably would have liked Twilight a lot more if it were a graphic novel in the style of Japanese manga or Korean manhwa, at least that's what I told myself when I thought about it after reading the whole series of books (despite having issues with the plot and pacing). It seemed like the kind of story that would be best suited for the drama. I've read many series over the years in those formats because I have a genuine love f</span>
  <span id="freeText10846783620345291331" style="display:none">You know what, if I'm allowed to be completely and utterly honest - I probably would have liked Twilight a lot more if it were a graphic novel in the style of Japanese manga or Korean manhwa, at least that's what I told myself when I thought about it after reading the whole series of books (despite having issues with the plot and pacing). It seemed like the kind of story that would be best suited for the drama. I've read many series over the years in those formats because I have a genuine love for some of the stories (Monster, NANA, etc.).<br /><br />Having said that, the announcement of Twilight's graphic novel adaptation came as a surprise - because I honestly didn't think it would come to fruition. When it did, I decided to let curiosity (as I'm prone to fall to) out of the bag and read the first volume. I'm really not a huge fan of Twilight, but I do give it credit where credit is due.<br /><br />I have mixed feelings about the GN overall, because on one hand - I think Young Kim's illustrations are very well done, brilliant even. I have no issues with the artwork at all, and surprisingly, the adaptation does match some of the impressions I had of the characters, Bella and Edward included. (Aside note - I wouldn't take Bella's beauty with too much critique - there are a lot of ordinary female protagonists in Asian graphic novels that actually look very beautiful in their artistic interpretations. It's a common trend.)<br /><br />The problems I had lie more in the technical execution of the graphic novel - the lettering was off, speaking bubbles shadowing over key characters, etc. It really could have been much better in presentation than what it was, and that did distract me. Considering this is an adaptation and not a direct serialization WRT the story - this was actually an interesting GN. I can't take away from it on that, and I'm usually very critical of such things like adaptations. It's at the very least consistent and gives a decent summarization of events for a good part of the GN (plot issues and characterization cliches aside).<br /><br />So in the end, I'm just giving it 3 stars. I spent about little more than an hour reading it and found it worth the time. But if I'm being honest - it's not worth the high price tag. If it were priced like most translated manga volumes, it would be worth it. If you're really concerned about the quality, I'd recommend checking it out if your local library has it, and then decide if its something you want to keep before you buy, because this might not be a book for everyone, even for those who are extremely dedicated to Twilight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10846783620345291331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6829409737660877094">Let me explain, first of all, that I LOVE graphic novels. When a particular novel really doesn't click, or I just really adored a book, I would try and find a graphic novel version. I had picked this book up one time at the store, curious about how it would be. I was well aware that I had learned little about the Twilight series prior to reading this, other than watching coming attractions in the movie theater over the years. <br/><br/>I was also aware that this, like so many popular books, has had some h</span>
  <span id="freeText6829409737660877094" style="display:none">Let me explain, first of all, that I LOVE graphic novels. When a particular novel really doesn't click, or I just really adored a book, I would try and find a graphic novel version. I had picked this book up one time at the store, curious about how it would be. I was well aware that I had learned little about the Twilight series prior to reading this, other than watching coming attractions in the movie theater over the years. <br /><br />I was also aware that this, like so many popular books, has had some haters and some lovers-- that the audience of readers is very split on whether this is a good or bad book. So I tried this book, with very unbiased opinion, from the library. <br /><br />Let me just say that I threw it across the room after the first 30 pages.<br /><br />Yes, it was that bad. I mean, the plotline was just plain badly imagined, poorly written, and some of the illustrations were quite obviously printed right on the page. Meaning, the backgrounds were not envisioned by the illustrator, but REAL PHOTOGRAPHS. Who DOES that???? Isn't that taking credit for someone else's work, just like using your name for something someone else did? Am I WRONG in thinking this?!?<br /><br />So, yeah. I would not, repeat WOULD NOT recommend this to anyone besides those too blinded by the love of a crappy, sodden-with-pointless-love-triangles plot to part with such a TERRIBLE book. Please, do spare me. I did myself when I returned this book, pronto. </span>

<div id="review_1923481468" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923481468" />
    <a title="Emm C²" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53296236-emm-c"><img alt="Emm C²" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558724665p2/53296236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923481468?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emm C²" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emm C²" href="/user/show/53296236-emm-c">Emm C²</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923481468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12676088570126648278">Hey, don't knock it 'til you try it. I wouldn't enjoy the novel, I know this. I don't have a visceral hatred of <i>Twilight</i> or anything, it's just that I'm sure it'd bore me. So I needn't bother just for the sake of saying I read it. The condensed, handsome graphic novel version of the doorstopper-length novel is a much faster read and retains what I know of the story. Good enough for me.<br/><br/>Vampires are more romantic than other human sanguivores, say zombies or cannibals - you never see cannibal roman</span>
  <span id="freeText12676088570126648278" style="display:none">Hey, don't knock it 'til you try it. I wouldn't enjoy the novel, I know this. I don't have a visceral hatred of <i>Twilight</i> or anything, it's just that I'm sure it'd bore me. So I needn't bother just for the sake of saying I read it. The condensed, handsome graphic novel version of the doorstopper-length novel is a much faster read and retains what I know of the story. Good enough for me.<br /><br />Vampires are more romantic than other human sanguivores, say zombies or cannibals - you never see cannibal romance novels, do you? But give me that over vampires. I enjoy vampire fiction but more along the horror edge and in small doses. <br />It's not terribly fair to fault works I know are not my forte I suppose, but <i>Twilight</i> tends to bypass the disturbing aspects being a vampire would come with in favour of the allure of eternal beauty (and <i>
  <b>sparkle</b>
</i> of course). Nevermind that Edward misuses his youth by redoing high school forty-thousand times...<br /><br />This is still surprisingly good though. I'm assuming it's more or less the same dialogue as the book. Again, it's not my favourite ever, but it's very much readable and I have to give Meyer kudos for trying to make a YA vampire romance that was a touch different from the norm. <i>Twilight</i>'s story works for a graphic medium, and Kim's art is honestly dazzling. Not much else to say, really!<br /><br />3.5/5</span>

<div id="review_202718274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202718274" />
    <a title="Julianna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/883725-julianna"><img alt="Julianna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442976820p2/883725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202718274?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna" href="/user/show/883725-julianna">Julianna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Twilight; Graphic Novel Adaptations</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/883725-julianna?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202718274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3862810811819231433">Reviewed for <a href='http://www.thcreviews.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>THC Reviews</a><br/><i>Twilight: The Graphic Novel, Volume 1</i> is pretty much what the title implies, the graphic novel adaptation of approximately the first half the <i>Twilight</i> novel. It covers Bella’s arrival in Forks, beginning school there, and meeting Edward. When Edward saves her from Tyler’s van nearly crushing her, she begins to suspect he’s not quite human. Eventually Edward decides to stop fighting his attraction to her, leading to him and Bella growing closer. After Bella visits La Push </span>
  <span id="freeText3862810811819231433" style="display:none">Reviewed for <a href="http://www.thcreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">THC Reviews</a><br /><i>Twilight: The Graphic Novel, Volume 1</i> is pretty much what the title implies, the graphic novel adaptation of approximately the first half the <i>Twilight</i> novel. It covers Bella’s arrival in Forks, beginning school there, and meeting Edward. When Edward saves her from Tyler’s van nearly crushing her, she begins to suspect he’s not quite human. Eventually Edward decides to stop fighting his attraction to her, leading to him and Bella growing closer. After Bella visits La Push Beach, meets Jacob, and hears the Quileute legends, she starts to form new theories of exactly what Edward is, and after he rescues her from would-be attackers in Port Angeles, they have much deeper conversations about it and about their budding relationship. The story winds up with Edward taking Bella to the meadow and revealing his true nature to her.<br /><br />The <i>Twilight</i> novel is a rather chunky book, so I’m sure it must be a challenge to pare it down to fit this short format. For that reason, I’d call this a respectable adaptation although one that is kind of bare bones. It hits all the high points nicely. However, there are so many details left out, it does feel a bit short on substance. True fans of the novels will easily be able to follow along, but I’m not as certain how the story might come off to someone who is exploring it for the first time in this format. As someone who’s read <i>Twilight</i> twice and seen the movie several times, it’s hard for me to gauge, because my brain automatically fills in any gaps. IMHO, what makes this graphic novel worthwhile, though, are the illustrations. Stephenie Meyer says that they come close to her vision of the characters, so I feel like I’m getting a peek into her mind’s eye. And beyond that, they’re quite simply beautiful and very well-done. I think that Young Kim did an excellent job of capturing the unearthly beauty of Edward and his family. In a more general sense, I liked the rendering of all the characters and felt that they matched well with my own vision of them. Bottom line, <i>Twilight: The Graphic Novel, Volume 1</i> is a must-have for hardcore fans of the book and collectors of Twilight merchandise. I enjoyed it for the lovely artwork and for a pretty good story adaptation and look forward to checking out the other graphic novels in the series, but newcomers should probably start with the novels to get the full impact of the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3862810811819231433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2572899345" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2572899345" />
    <a title="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile"><img alt="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546974316p2/7494844.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2572899345?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" href="/user/show/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile">laurel [the suspected bibliophile]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=omfg-awful">omfg-awful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2572899345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7655371774167680916"><b>DNF at 40 pages</b><br/><br/>I-I just, no? Okay?<br/><br/>Maybe in high school? But probably then, probably even not.<br/><br/>This takes everything that was halfway decent in the books, shits on it, and continues with the crappiest of poopooness.<br/><br/>Right from the beginning, Bella is self-sacrificing to the max. She's selflessly giving her life up for someone else in the prologue, she's exiling herself to rainy and poopy Forks, Washington, so that her mother and step-father can have a new life together, and she is...well, she's jus</span>
  <span id="freeText7655371774167680916" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 40 pages</b><br><br>I-I just, no? Okay?<br><br>Maybe in high school? But probably then, probably even not.<br><br>This takes everything that was halfway decent in the books, shits on it, and continues with the crappiest of poopooness.<br><br>Right from the beginning, Bella is self-sacrificing to the max. She's selflessly giving her life up for someone else in the prologue, she's exiling herself to rainy and poopy Forks, Washington, so that her mother and step-father can have a new life together, and she is...well, she's just a wet dishrag of a human being.<br><br>It's a little much, particularly when the self-exile isn't explained and has Bella coming off as more whiny, angsty, spoiled teenager than anything. Her constant bitching about the weather, the rain, the tininess of the town and the school, her bedroom, her truck, her father, her friends-that-can't-be-friends-because-they're-not-the-mysterious-and-gorgeous-Cullens, the Cullens' ancient names (okay, <i>Isabella</i>), it's just...I just want to shake her and shout, "Bloom where you're planted!" Or...at least keep the griping to yourself?<br><br>Talk about a buzzkill.<br><br>Then there's the Gary Stu in vampire form: Edward Cullens.<br><br>His anger practically oozes off the page. His fists are always clenched, he's always staring at her. Even when he's "nice" he's still a colossal dickhead.<br><br>And of course Bella is absolutely intrigued by this man that she's angered with her mere existence.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540467881ra/26499054.gif" width="200" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, some things that I've apparently overlooked in the book because it's been so long since I've read the first one (or the rest) and I've purged the story from my mind:<br><br>1. How long has Charlie been the sheriff of Forks?<br><br>2. If all of the things in Bella's room are hers, how come she's not familiar with the town? Did her Dad move there after the divorce? When was the divorce anyway?<br><br>3. Why the hell did Bella move away from Phoenix?<br><br>4. How come she doesn't know any of the kids in Forks since she's apparently spent some time up there beforehand?<br><br>5. How come none of the Cullens "children" have been reported to a substance abuse program?<br><br>6. And the enduring question that has haunted me ever since the release of the first book so many, many years ago:<br><br><b>WHY THE FUCK WOULD 100 YEAR OLD VAMPIRES VOLUNTARILY <i>CHOOSE</i> TO GO BACK TO HIGH SCHOOL OF ALL THE DAMN PLACES?!?!?!!?!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540467545ra/26499018.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Hi, I'm Edward, your local cannibalistic pedophile :)</i><br><br><b>GO TO COLLEGE AND USE YOUR MONEY TO GET ALL THE DEGREES!</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and hey, at least in college the girls are legal, right? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>*sigh* why did I do this to myself?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RMmF/XXlAsi5EAt6mnkrgiFfuHvHTzR/jHiqj+euY+DhYpjRgKi7sjSS91MeD19nnL8Xns4Ail4rduBl1UgSLg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V3Idpq5LUoUxWT0urqdGy7tIlSCcyOrf/YBdeJtj8S7y2QCKWwbr/7zbwQcq0TIuBqg6xZWHVP5ajheSqYWA4A==')})
  }
//]]>

The characters of the Twilight Saga carry a rich history that shapes their identities and actions over the course of the series. Edward, for instance, may look like a seventeen-year-old teen heartthrob, but was actually born in 1901 and died during the Spanish Influenza of 1918. His adopted sister, Alice, was imprisoned in an insane asylum in 1920 and treated so badly there that even becoming a vampire was a welcome escape. This book is the first to explore the history behind the Twilight Saga\'s characters and their stories. You’ll learn about what life might have been like for Jasper Whitlock Hale, the Confederate vampire who fought during the Civil War, Carlisle Cullen, the Puritan witch hunter-turned-vampire who participated in the witchcraft persecutions in Early Modern England, and the history of the Quileute culture that shaped Jacob and his people —and much more.\n\n\nGives you the historical backdrop for Twilight Saga characters and events\nAdds a whole new dimension to the Twilight novels and movies\nOffers fresh insights on vampires, romance, and history\n\nTwilight and History is an essential companion for every Twilight fan, whether you\'ve just gotten into the series or have followed it since the beginning.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"17915577305190003502\" href=\"#\"
